## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: population ecology / population dynamics
**Analysis**: This task models the population growth rate dP/dt as a function of time t and population P, which is the fundamental problem of population dynamics. The growth rate typically depends on current population through density-dependent mechanisms, and may have explicit time dependence through seasonal or environmental changes.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Exponential growth: dP_dt = c0 * P (density-independent unlimited growth)
- Logistic growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) (density-dependent growth with carrying capacity)
- Gompertz growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * log(c1 / P) (growth rate decreasing logarithmically with population)
- Allee effect (strong): dP_dt = c0 * P * (P - c1) * (1 - c2 * P) (growth negative below critical threshold)
- Theta-logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) (generalized logistic with shape parameter)
- Von Bertalanffy-type: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 - c2 * P (anabolism-catabolism balance)
- Richards growth: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - (c1 * P)**c2) / c2 (flexible sigmoidal growth)
- Time-varying exponential: dP_dt = c0 * P * exp(c1 * t) (growth rate changing exponentially with time)
- Logistic with time-varying rate: dP_dt = c0 * exp(c1 * t) * P * (1 - c2 * P) (seasonal or trending growth rate)
- Power-law growth: dP_dt = c0 * P**c1 (fractional power density dependence)
- Harvesting/immigration logistic: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P) + c2 (logistic with constant immigration or harvesting)
- Oscillatory carrying capacity: dP_dt = c0 * P * (1 - c1 * P * (1 + c2 * sin(c3 * t))) (seasonal carrying capacity)
- Quadratic density dependence: dP_dt = c0 * P + c1 * P**2 + c2 * P**3 (polynomial density effects)
- Beverton-Holt continuous: dP_dt = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) - c2 * P (saturating birth rate with linear death)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Density dependence (negative feedback) → Terms like P*(1 - c*P) or P*(K-P) indicating self-limiting growth as resources deplete
- Allee effect (positive density dependence at low P) → Cubic terms P*(P-c1)*(c2-P) creating growth rate that is negative at very low populations
- Metabolic scaling in growth → Power-law terms P**c with fractional exponents (e.g., c=2/3 or 3/4) reflecting surface-to-volume or metabolic scaling
- Compensatory vs depensatory mortality → Whether per-capita rate dP_dt/P is monotonically decreasing (compensatory) or has a hump shape (depensatory) in P
- Separability test → If dP_dt = f(P)*g(t), the dynamics are separable and time acts as a modulator of intrinsic population-dependent dynamics
- Carrying capacity signature → Growth rate crosses zero at a specific P value, indicating equilibrium; mathematically dP_dt has a root at P=K
- Immigration/refuge terms → Constant additive terms (independent of P) suggest immigration, emigration, or stocking in population models
- Phase-plane structure → If dP_dt depends only on P (not t), the system is autonomous and trajectories are determined by P alone, suggesting time-invariant environment
